Feature | IRM-32912 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | RELIABILITY | Data Integrity improvements. Error handling in synchronous operations that involve distributed transactions / Registry, Taxpayer | Other | PI28 | 1493.1 | p1 | HLD | cont.  :https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-25038 

 

Solon Tax microservices have domain boundaries that also encapsulate the corresponding transactional boundaries. I.e. most API operations result in ACID transactions as the updates are handled within the owning microservice's database.

 

However there are some APIs of the system that the owning service also issues PUT/POST requests to different services. For these cases, strong error handling should be introduced.

 

Syncronous operations refer to:
 * HTTP api invocation. A distributed transaction there involves data updates to more than one microservices in the lifecycle of the HTTP request
 * Kafka message consumption. A distributed transaction there involves data updates to more than one microservices in the lifecycle of the kafka message under consuption.

In cases were an operation invokes one or more published messages that are subsequently causing other updates, these are considere eventually consistent transactions and are not in the scope of this enabler.

 

Scope of this enabler is to :

Decide and introduce appropriate error handling for Taxpayer cases as listed in [https://netcompany.sharepoint.com/:x:/s/ICARUSProductTeam/IQDDvVCJsRcQR5si6csRQX4UASFBtrUfVPMWEu6yVXFAQ6w?e=6ZruVa] 
*for " taxpayer", "registration"* 

Consider any patterns to the flows implemented already

Note that the [https://confluence.intrasoft-intl.com/spaces/IC/pages/224722770/Data+integrity+improvements]  

1. Assign worker to a human task.
2. Claim a human task
Feature | IRM-30255 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | MAINTAINABILITY | Support an AI-assisted JSON schema generation mechanism within Form Designer | Other | PI30 | 1213.1 | p3 | Under Analysis | As an admin, I should be able to use an AI-assisted JSON + UI schemas generation mechanism when using the form designer, so as to minimise complexity and error prone methods.

*Introduction* 

Adding an AI-assisted JSON schema generation mechanism within the Form Designer would significantly reduce complexity for administrators, developers, and integrators by automatically converting designed forms into standardized data structures.

*Functional Requirement* 

*> AI Schema Translation*

Revenue Management shall automatically generate a JSON Schema representation for every saved or published form.

Revenue Management shall use an AI model to infer correct JSON Schema types, structures, and validation constraints based on field definitions and properties from the form designer.

_Example:_ A “Date of Birth” field becomes {{{}{ "type": "string", "format": "date" }{}}}.

Revenue Management shall support bidirectional conversion, allowing import of JSON Schemas back into editable form layouts.

The AI engine shall recognize conditional logic and field dependencies and express them in JSON Schema constructs (e.g., {{{}if/then/else{}}}).

The AI engine shall automatically infer relationships between nested sections or tabs and map them as nested JSON objects.

*> Schema Optimization and Validation*

The AI engine shall validate generated JSON Schemas for compliance with JSON Schema Draft version specifications compatible with the one used in solon Tax revenue management at the time.

Revenue Management shall flag inconsistencies or redundant structures detected during generation (e.g., duplicate field names, circular dependencies).

Revenue Management shall allow users to preview and manually fine-tune the generated JSON Schema before publishing.

Revenue Management shall maintain version history for generated schemas aligned with form versions.

*> AI Learning and Context Awareness*

The AI engine shall learn from existing published forms and schemas to improve accuracy of future translations (e.g., reusing known field mappings).

The AI engine shall support domain-specific language understanding — for instance, recognizing that “Gross Income” or “Taxable Income” should be treated as numeric fields with precision settings.

The AI shall support multilingual form labels, understanding that language differences should not affect schema consistency.

*> Integration and Export*

Revenue Management shall allow exporting the generated JSON Schema for use in external systems (e.g., data validation APIs or ETL processes).

Revenue Management shall expose a REST API endpoint to retrieve schema definitions programmatically by form name or version.

The AI mechanism shall ensure backward compatibility between schema versions (e.g., mapping old field names to new ones if renamed).

*> Security and Governance*

The AI mechanism shall not expose sensitive taxpayer data during schema generation or learning.

Revenue Management shall record an audit log of AI actions (generation, corrections, user overrides).

Only users with specific roles can configure, view or export generated schemas.

Feature | IRM-37610 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | MAINTAINABILITY | Restructure revenue-management-be-custom to align with Hexagonal Architecture | Other | PI29 | 193.89999999999998 | p3 | To Do | h3. Problem Statement

The current module structure of *revenue-management-be-custom* is not aligned with hexagonal architecture principles.

Hexagonal architecture is the architectural foundation of the *SolonTax* and the same principles should consistently apply to {*}be-custom{*}.

At present, the structure does not clearly separate application, domain, and adapter layers, which makes the module harder to maintain, evolve, and use as a proper extension point.

Since *be-custom* is intended to serve clients as a starting point for implementing their own platform customizations, the current structure does not provide a clean and consistent reference model to follow.
h3. Proposed Solution

Restructure *revenue-management-be-custom* to follow hexagonal architecture principles and align it with the architectural standards of the main *revenue-management-be* project.

The target modular structure should consist of:
 * microservice-adapter
 * microservice-app
 * microservice-core
 * microservice-rest-api
 * microservice-dto (optional)
 * microservice-domain (optional)
 * microservice-business-specific (optional, more than one module possible)

Module dependencies should follow the structure presented in the attached diagram: 

!image-2026-02-26-14-41-24-169.png!
h3. Out of Scope
 * Introduction of new business functionality.
 * Refactoring of unrelated microservices.
 * Major redesign of existing business logic beyond structural alignment.
 * Changes in external APIs or contracts unless required by the restructuring.

h3. PPD Maturity Index / Control point: Quality / Maintainability / Modularity
Feature | IRM-38847 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | SECURITY | Data Security - Restrict Access to Personal Data GDPR- Admin (based on data classifications) - Encrypt/decrypt -  Part 4/4 | Other | PI28 | 42.4 | p3 | To Do | cont, [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-20329] 
depends on https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-20328 

As an admin, I want to restrict access to sensitive personal data, so that only users that have a legitimate reason to access this data are granted access and unauthorized access to this data is prevented.

*Introduction*

This feature is related to the epic IRM-3106 in which requirements have been documented to secure the information in the revenue management system from unauthorized access.

This feature is related to IRM-30322 in which requirements have been documented to classify fields (or characteristics or categories of attachments) in the application as fields that contain non-personal, personal or sensitive personal data GDPR. However, not each field that has been classified to contain (sensitive) personal data will always contain personal data, as these fields (e.g. identifier or address fields) may also be used to record data for parties that are not natural persons. Only if the data in these fields is related to a natural person (see IRM-20315), it can be considered personal data. Exception to this rule is data that cannot be related to or has not yet been related to a specific party, such as data in forms, uploaded payment data or messages in the message store that cannot or not yet be related to a specific party. This data should be considered personal if the data has been classified as such.

*Functional Requirements*
 * Admin can choose to show or hide encrypted personal data on the user interface for users that do not have access to the decrypted sensitive personal data
 * Admin can define that decrypted personal data is shown on the user interface for users that do have access to the decrypted sensitive personal data
 * {color:#172b4d}Admin should be able to encrypt personal data details from logs (audit)/exception/message store , data areas, notes, forms, cases/ human task comments.{color}

 

*Documentation*
Document all the above adjustments. 

 

*Non functional requirements*
It is expected to reassure that relevant NFRs (Performance , Security, Accessibility, Usability ) are tested and are not negatively affecting the product.  
DODs should be fulfilled.

Feature | IRM-30730 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | MAINTAINABILITY | Introduce helm charts dependencies | Other | PI30 | 392 | p3 | To Do | *Problem Statement*

The current Helm chart architecture for SolonTax does not utilize Helm's dependency mechanism. This has led to several inefficiencies:
 * *Template Duplication:* Common templates and helper logic are copied across multiple charts, leading to significant code duplication.
 * *High Maintenance Overhead:* Enhancements or bug fixes made in one chart's templates must be manually identified and ported to all other charts, a process that is both time-consuming and error-prone.
 * *Inconsistent Configurations:* The {{revenue-management-be}} and {{revenue-management-be-custom}} charts are maintained as two completely separate entities, doubling the effort required for updates and increasing the risk of divergence.

This lack of a centralized structure makes the charts difficult to maintain, scale, and audit.

*Proposed Solution*

This feature will refactor the SolonTax Helm charts to adopt a more modular and maintainable structure by introducing a common *{{base}}* chart.
 # *Create a {{base}} Helm Chart:* A new {{base}} chart will be created to serve as a common dependency for all application charts. This chart will consolidate all shared templates, helpers, and logic (e.g., for Deployments, Services, ConfigMaps, etc.). It will be designed to be flexible enough to handle both backend and frontend components.

 # *Refactor {{revenue-management-be}} Charts:* The {{revenue-management-be-custom}} chart will be refactored to use the {{revenue-management-be}} chart as a parent dependency. The custom chart will become a lightweight extension, responsible only for overriding values (like image tags) and adding configurations specific to the customized microservices. This will result in a single, unified Helm release for all {{revenue-management-be}} components.

*Acceptance Criteria*
 # *Base Chart Creation:* A new {{base}} Helm chart is created and contains common, reusable templates for standard Kubernetes resources (e.g., Deployment, Service, ConfigMap, Ingress).
 # *Dependency Adoption:* All existing SolonTax application charts (both backend and frontend) are updated to declare the {{base}} chart as a dependency in their {{{}Chart.yaml{}}}.
 # *Duplication Removal:* Duplicated template logic is removed from the application charts, which now leverage the templates provided by the {{base}} chart.
 # *{{revenue-management-be}} Refactoring:* The {{revenue-management-be-custom}} chart is refactored to be a child chart of {{{}revenue-management-be{}}}.
 # *Unified Release:* A single {{helm install}} or {{helm upgrade}} of the refactored {{revenue-management-be-custom}} chart successfully deploys both the standard {{revenue-management-be}} components and the customized components as a single Helm release.
 # *Override Functionality:* The {{revenue-management-be-custom}} chart can successfully override default values (e.g., image tags) from the parent {{revenue-management-be}} chart and inject additional properties for its specific microservices.
 # *Flexibility for Exceptions:* Application charts retain the ability to introduce their own specialized templates if a specific requirement cannot be met by the common {{base}} chart.
Feature | IRM-30730 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | MAINTAINABILITY | Introduce helm charts dependencies | Other | PI29 | 42 | p3 | To Do | *Problem Statement*

The current Helm chart architecture for SolonTax does not utilize Helm's dependency mechanism. This has led to several inefficiencies:
 * *Template Duplication:* Common templates and helper logic are copied across multiple charts, leading to significant code duplication.
 * *High Maintenance Overhead:* Enhancements or bug fixes made in one chart's templates must be manually identified and ported to all other charts, a process that is both time-consuming and error-prone.

Feature | IRM-20329 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | SECURITY | Data Security - Restrict Access to Personal Data GDPR- Admin (based on data classifications) - Part 1/4 | Other | PI28 | 1217.3 | p2 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As an admin, I want to restrict access to sensitive personal data, so that only users that have a legitimate reason to access this data are granted access and unauthorized access to this data is prevented.

*Introduction*

This feature is related to the epic IRM-3106 in which requirements have been documented to secure the information in the revenue management system from unauthorized access.

This feature is related to IRM-30322 in which requirements have been documented to classify fields  (or characteristics or categories of attachments) in the application as fields that contain non-personal, personal or sensitive personal data GDPR. However, not each field that has been classified to contain (sensitive) personal data will always contain personal data, as these fields (e.g. identifier or address fields) may also be used to record data for parties that are not natural persons. Only if the data in these fields is related to a natural person (see IRM-20315), it can be considered personal data. Exception to this rule is data that cannot be related to or has not yet been related to a specific party, such as data in forms, uploaded payment data or messages in the message store that cannot or not yet be related to a specific party. This data should be considered personal if the data has been classified as such.
Depends on [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-20322] 

 

*Out of scope :* 
Archive db
Define classifications for financial details and relevant datasets (see [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-23836] )

 

+Clarifications:+
classify fields  : as discussed  we mean restrict access to records based on record type and defined classification levels 

+Expected Behaviors to be available :+ 
+Visibility:+ 
Field masking, e.g. Name = *****
Record hidden , e.g. record not returned
+Search+
Record hidden, e.g., No results returned, Result excluded completely
Field masking,  e.g., Result returned but masked
+Logs+
Logs should be immutable. Information may be masked. 
 

*Functional Requirements*

*For Party , Party Roles, Attachments:*  
 * Admin can restrict access to sensitive personal data based on classification level and group of users (e.g. using user access groups).
The classification levels are defined in  [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-20322] 

 * Admin can restrict based on classification levels, who can :
 ** _Create_
 ** _Read ( 2 modes to be able to be configured :  masked or not listing the record)_ 
 ** _Update_  
 ** _Delete_
 ** _Search_ 
 ** The above permissions must be enforceable for operations initiated via the UI, direct service calls, or APIs.
_Suggestion:  Data Access Layer Enforcement of permissions_
 **  __ It is expected that the visibility of the classified details may be configured by configurators as : masked or non visible. (see also ILs)

 * Admin should be able to remove (masking or removing record visibility)  access of records based on classification levels, from data areas of Party,  party role, Attachments

+Examples:+ 
An Admin can successfully configure a User Access Group to have "Read" access to "Personal Data" but be denied "Read" access to "Sensitive Personal Data".
When a user from that group views a list of parties, parties with only "Personal Data" are visible, while parties with "Sensitive Personal Data" are either hidden or have their sensitive fields masked, as configured.
When the same user performs a search, the results correctly exclude or mask records containing "Sensitive Personal Data".

*{color:#172b4d}Identification Labels{color}*
 * {color:#172b4d}Identification labels should be displayed according the relevant classifications restrictions. 
E.g. : If the identifier used in IL (i.e. the primary) is sensitive and not visible by user  (John Takis, Tax Identification Number: 123456789) 
a) if the mode is to mask sensitive detail -> IL appears with stars instead of identifier. (John Takis, Tax Identification Number: ********** )
b) if the mode is that the data should not appear in the results -> IL appears  with empty details  (John Takis, Tax Identification Number:  ){color}{color:#172b4d}Similarly in other ILs related with classified data. {color}

{color:#172b4d}*Message store*{color}
 * {color:#172b4d}Admin should be able to remove (masking or removing record visibility)  access of records based on classification levels, from Message store. Permission set as per above mentioned list (view, search ,etc.).{color}

*{color:#172b4d}Operational Reports{color}*
 * {color:#172b4d}Visibility of records in Operational reports are restricted (masking or removing record visibility) based on above mentioned classification levels and permissions. {color}

*{color:#172b4d}Other related entities/cross-entity propagation{color}*
 * {color:#172b4d}Restrictions must propagate to any entity that displays or uses classified data.
Visibility of records in all system records*  are restricted (masking or removing record visibility) based on above mentioned classification levels and permissions.
*Examples :  {color}

 * 
 ** Forms,
 ** Cases,
 ** Human task,
 ** Taxpayer accounts related (e.g. : liabilities, bill segments, bills, Fts, Journal entries, suppression, assessments)
 ** Registration related (e.g. : Candidate lists, Operational Plans, Calendar records - timeoff, assignments-, Organizational units , Asset relationships,  revenue type Registrations, Obligations, user right) 
 ** Users, user roles,  Object access groups
 ** Notifications
 ** Contacts
 ** Notes

 

*Governance* 
The permissions will be defined by admin as described In [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-39113] 

 

*Documentation*
Document all the above adjustments. 

 

*Non functional requirements*
It is expected to reassure that relevant NFRs (Performance , Security, Accessibility, Usability ) are tested and are not negatively affecting the product.  
DODs should be fulfilled.

Feature | IRM-33406 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | MAINTAINABILITY | Integrate Self-Contained Documentation Portal into Solon Tax Deliverable | Other | PI29 | 448 | p3 | To Do | As a Solon Tax user on a customer-hosted environment, I want to access relevant help documentation directly from the Solon Tax hosted environment, so that I can get assistance without needing seperate access to connect to {{[https://docs.netcompany.com/]}} site

*Description:*

Currently, the Solon Tax UI integrates with the internal documentation portal at {{{}[https://docs.netcompany.com/]{}}}. This setup is not desired for customer-premise deployments which are often in isolated environments.

This story covers the work required to package, deploy, and integrate a self-contained version of the Solon Tax documentation portal within the standard Solon Tax product deliverables.

*Acceptance Criteria:*
 # A new process exists to build a stripped-down Docker image of the documentation portal, containing only the Solon Tax documentation.
 # A new Helm chart is created to deploy this documentation Docker image as part of the standard Solon Tax vanilla deployment.
 # The Solon Tax UI is reconfigured to retrieve help pages from the newly deployed, in-cluster documentation service instead of the external {{{}docs.netcompany.com{}}}.
 # Access to the bundled documentation site is secured; users must be authenticated and authorized through the existing Solon Tax access control mechanisms.
 # Unauthenticated users are prevented from accessing the documentation content.
 # Documentation on installation deliverables, installation procedure and architecture are updated accordingly.

Feature | IRM-30360 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | SECURITY | Data visibility permissions / Row level access, per hierarchical level of users in teams | GRC | PI28 | 132 | p1 | To Do | As an admin I need to reassure that permissions of some of the system records are assigned hierarchical. 

In system Organizational Hierarchy will be implemented via Organizational Units, where a permission level role is assigned. 

The row level security will initially define the restrictions on records visibility. The hierarchical permissions will now grant permissions when restricted by row level. 

*Introduction*

The hierarchy is expected to be implemented introducing in higher levels leaders that to get leader permissions should be flagged as "Task Assigner " (It is permitted to add members but permissions should  be defined) 
Higher levels may have visibility permissions to records of the defined types  of the lower records of the same branch. Will not have access to the other branched unless records are publicly visible. 

Note that some of the below permissions, can be achieved by OPA rules in row level security.  
!image-2025-10-09-19-58-53-208.png|width=292,height=349!

 

 

*Functional Requirements*

While adding users under Organization units,  the permissions managed in hierarchy level should be defined. 
 * *Entity/Record types  to be affected Hierarchically by Org Units :*
 ** Time off requests : Permissions on CRUD, Assignments, Approvals based on user's Organization for Time Off requests
 ** Human Task (Assignments ):  Permission to Assign 
 ** Cases (Assignments ):  Permission to Assign 
 ** Users (Visibility)  : visibility of details 
 ** Resource Calendars : Permissions to see assigned calendar details 

 * *Default Visibility & Ownerships*
Owner/Mine  : I am assigner or the user that represents this record
Manager: I am in higher hierarchy "IS HEAD"
 ** The above users (owner, manager) gain by default read access to records.
 ** i.e. per entity: 
Human Tasks, Cases :  a) Assigned to Human task or b) if unassigned , eligible user or manager of eligible user
User : User + Manager
Resource Calendars : Assigned user  + Manager
Time off requests : Requestor /User  + Manager
 ** The users not assigned to any category does not have visibility to records. 

 * *Sharing Assignments Permissions per Hierarchy levels per Organizational Level* **
 ** Lower level same branch -> permissions  for the users assigned below in hierarchy
 ** Same level same branch  -> permissions  for the users assigned in same level of hierarchy
 ** Higher level same branch or top level -> permissions  for the users assigned higher in hierarchy
 ** Same level Different branch
 ** Higher level Different branch or top level
 ** Lower level Different branch 
 ** Mine - see above
 ** Admin : a special permission to see and modify all
 ** Permissions may be combined if user is assigned to several org units 
 * *Permissions* 
 ** *Read* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)  /  *DEFAULT PERMISSIONS when IS HEAD*
 ** *Assign* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)
 ** *Approve* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)
 ** *Edit* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)
 ** *Cancel* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)
 ** *Delegate Tasks* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)

 

*Examples :* 

if the categories are like that and should be combined in a matrix

Feature | IRM-30561 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | MAINTAINABILITY | After POC - Config Items Management ( Packaging & versioning) : Enable delivery teams to safely and selectively migrate configurations across environments /WIP | GRC | PI29 | 11946.9 | p3 | To Do | *AFTER POC*  [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-29268] 

{color:#ff8b00}*WIP  - Will be defined after POC* {color}
----
As a Solon Tax Delivery team, I need to be able to: 
-  safely and selectively, via guided steps, to migrate configurations across environments (Dev → Stg → Prod),
-  maintain versions of the configurations/other artifacts migrated to other environments and of the release/migration  (e.g. artifact version, release version)   
-  provide report on the results of the deployment process, 
-  see the history of the migrations, 
-  support zero/near-zero downtime deployments   (?)
-  support scheduled activation/ make effective the changes to destination environment,
-  enable team to flag changes as "ready to be migrated" , and capture ownership details
-  filter in a longer list of items based on predefine flags or versions the items to be added in the package for the migration,
-  enable team to select,  implementations, supporting them with  prechecks (Pre‑checks: environment compatibility, dependency resolution, conflict detection, schema compatibility, dry‑run simulation), dependencies and conflicts checks, 
-  provide rollback and recovery options,
-  enable team to select source and destination environments, 
-  ensure security, performance,  and compliance,
-  enforce governance with roles, performance and approval flows.

 

*Background:*
 
Configuration Data
 * Entity types (c_ objects) , Codelists/codelist items, , System parameters (codelist item attributes), 
queries, other config data (users, exchange rates, calendars, worker profiles, roles, object access groups, user access groups, ledgers, GL accounts numbers, rates etc), UI schemas/forms.'

Translations
 * Labels ( _l objects) 

TBC: 
 * (?) User defined characteristics,
 * Drools
 * (?) Other customizations

Ownerships 
 * Config items are flagged with its ownership , i.e. :  on who is responsible for their maintenance (Product team, national delivery team, or client-specific team) restricting areas that should not be used,  their intended scope of usage / applicability (global, regional, or specific clients) , whether they are reusable across implementations Additionally provide controlling mechanism on which items based on owner are eligible to be migrated (e.g. do not deploy base items, unless it is an attribute of a system parameter, entity schema help url, or labels.)   [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-26335]  

*Functional Requirements:*

*+Preparation+* 
 * *Prerequisites*
 ** Define environments that can be source and destinations
 ** Define the versioning numbering that will be used for all the items (?)
 * *Flag configuration items*
 ** Beforehand, the developer/admin should label Ownership of the component. 
 ** Beforehand, the developer/admin may label configurations implemented as  "Ready for export".  ([https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/PSD-11032)|https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/PSD-11032])
 ** Beforehand, version of the items to be migrated may be defined. 
 ** Beforehand, the developer/admin optionally may label the component with the Functionality or Scope or Product component will support.  
 ** Beforehand, the developer/admin may select if the Cong items will be activated while migrated or will remain inactive till admin manually activate them the destination environment. 
 ** Beforehand, the developer/admin may upload the file where applicable (labels - translations) should be uploaded. 
 ** Beforehand, the developer/admin may select the source and destination environments.  

 * *Roles and permissions*
 ** Permitted users can use the packaging tool and perform the mentioned actions

              consideration :  ? Could it be extended to use approval processes?

 

*+Core+*
 * *Ui*
 ** Admin may see the details of previous local releases/ deployments as well as historical data on the local releases/ deployments
 ** Admin/developer may check out and then check in any non Base config item
 *** Checked in item receives automatically a version
 *** Validation when trying to check out a Base item
 ** Admin may initiate a new deployment (create release) 
 *** Select source and destination environment
 *** UI or CLI to *select/export/inspect/import* configurations, code, flows, templates, etc.
 *** Select to proceed with the deployment
 *** Admin may use filters  (as per flags added above , version number ,  along with other items e.g. category field) to locate the items to be included in the package. 
 *** Admin can add comments per item and per local release. 
 ** Admin may see details under each logged release
 *** Admin can see timestamp and historical details on the local release. 
 *** Admin can see list of exceptions before and after the deployment
 ** Admin after deployment will be able to make effective/enable the version/selected items in destination environment. 

 

+*Deployment process*+

 
 * *Suggest items to be selected*
 ** Provide Delta support to select elements that are new or modified -  where applicable.
 ** Exclude BASE items with exceptions (help urls, labels, attributes in system parameters).
 ** Indicate possible conflicts.
 * *Dependency management*  - Select items to be migrated (metadata, content ... ) from a list .
 ** Identify dependencies and indicate what related items need to move together.
Identify and warn if related components must be exported together.
 ** Support  when certain settings (like endpoint URLs, external credentials, currency precision) may need to differ by environment - need a way to parameterize or externalize environment-specific config.)

 * *Standard Format & Packaging*
 ** Define a standard export/import format   (e.g., JSON, XML, YAML or other per component type) 
 ** Group exported artifacts into packages. 
 ** Be able to define the expiration date / inactivation date of an older version per component and have available mechanisms to validate that the new version will be available when old is expired. 
 *  *Import & Validation* : 
 ** Examine if needs to define states for each deployable (e.g., {_}Draft → Approved → Deployed → Deprecated{_}).
 ** Ensure compatibility and prevent unintended overwrites.
 ** Run automated validations in a dry run mode
 ** Indicate possible conflicts.
 ** Simulate a deployment before actual promotion
 ** Advice smoke testing after deployment

 * *Auditability and Reporting* 
 ** Audit Trail of  who changed what, when, and where in the target environment. (See also relevant section on  [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-27058] ) 
 ** Be able to see the result of the migration process. Monitor what succeeded, failed, or was skipped.
 
 * *Rollback Mechanism  / go back to a previous version*  
 ** Ability to revert a deployment if needed either fully or selectively.  See also relevant section on  [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-27058] 
 ** Ability to set when old version should be expired as new version should be active.  See also relevant section on  [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-27058] 

 * Compliance/ *Data security* privacy (Certain configuration or integration artifacts may handle sensitive data)
 ** Dev and Stg environments are created without taxpayer data, but include configuration and custom logic. i.e.,  when exporting from production to other envs, do not deploy data. 
 * Other
 ** Consider also translation management needs as described in  IRM-24809  

 

 

*Documentation*
 * Documentation will be delivered with the steps to install the application and tools needed plus how to use the tool with example. 

*Non Functional Requirements:*
 * Tool can be handled by delivery teams.
 * Performance and security DODs should be considered.

*Functional Requirements*
 * Admin can define user-defined characteristics that must be available for a payment event
 * Admin can edit the properties of a user-defined characteristics, such as a unique identifier, description, help text, data type, data length, predefined value, lookup values, required, visible, and display only. Examples of data types that can be supported for these characteristics are string, date/time, number, amount, code list (e.g. region) and a reference to another type of entity in the application.
 * Reference Type of Entity
 ** Admin can define multiple user-defined characteristics that reference the same type of entity if instances of that type of entity can have a different meaning for a payment event
 ** Admin can define whether a user-defined characteristic can reference only one or multiple instances of a specific type of entity
 ** Admin can define what properties are shown for each type of entity that is referenced by a certain user-defined characteristic
 * Reference Code List
 ** Admin can define multiple user-defined characteristics that reference the same code list
 ** Admin can define whether a user-defined characteristic can reference only one or multiple code list items of a specific code list
 * Admin can remove a user-defined characteristic for a payment event if there are no referential constraints
 * Admin can disable a user-defined characteristic for a payment event if the characteristic is no longer relevant
 * Admin can enable a disabled user-defined characteristic for a payment event if the characteristic is deemed relevant again
 * Admin should be warned when adding or editing user-defined characteristics when payment events exist
 * Grouping
 ** Admin can group characteristics. Group can contain sub-groups.
 ** Admin can edit a group, for example the description
 ** Admin can delete a group, provided there are no referential constraints
 ** User can rearrange groups and sub-groups
 ** User can rearrange the characteristics within the payment event, groups or sub-groups
 * Rules
 ** Admin can define rules for a characteristic to validate the data that will be entered by the user
 ** Admin can define rules for a characteristic to determine if the characteristic should be visible or invisible
 ** Admin can define rules for a characteristic to determine if a characteristic is required or not
 ** Admin can define rules for a characteristic to determine when the characteristic should be editable or not
 ** Admin can define an error message that must be shown when the data entered by the user does not comply with the validation rule

Feature | IRM-29430 | CORE REVENUE MANAGEMENT CAPABILITIES | PENALTY & INTEREST | Enhance Credit Interest Calculation to include unallocated payment segments | GTM | PI28 | 2986.9 | p2 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As a revenue authority officer I would like Solon RM to consider in credit interest calculation, all payments received from a taxpayer, both allocated and unallocated, so that final interest calculation is accurate and can be used in relevant processes.  

*Introduction*
This feature was originally introduced for SKV implementation of Reimbursement Interest in [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-15910] the credits from Bill segments are considered in the calculations. To complete this interest calculation, system needs to consider all payment segments as well. 

Moving forward for the implemetation of the Tax Account in Northern countries but also for other implementations, in order to calculate interest accurately all payment segments, allocated and unallocated needs to be considered.  

Update the existing CREDIT_INT PI (Penalty & Interest) rule to calculate reimbursement interest on credit unallocated payment segments for tax account scenarios, ensures taxpayers receive proper interest on all credit amounts.

Currently, the system calculates interest only on bill segment balances. However, when for example liability amendments occur (e.g., reducing a VAT liability from €100 to €80 after a €100 payment has been made), the resulting €20 credit unallocated payment segment does not accrue interest in favor of the taxpayer. This creates an unfair situation where taxpayer funds held by the tax authority do not earn the required interest. 

To enhance understanding of this feature and facilitate analysis tasks please find below a business example as well as business cases where Solon Tax results in unallocated payment segments.

*System Requirements*
 * PI Rule Enhancement: Rule Code = CREDIT_INT (Reimbursement Interest Rule) Enhancement: Update calculation logic to include credit unallocated payment segments (next to credits on bill segments that is already implemented). 

*Business Example*

> Initial State:

VAT Liability: €100 (debit)

Payment Made: €100 (credit)

Result: Liability fully paid, balance = €0

> After Amendment:

Amendment: VAT liability reduced by €20 (becomes €80)

Payment Remains: €100 (unchanged)

Result: €20 credit unallocated payment segment

_Current Behavior:_

Interest calculated only on bill segment balances, thus €20 credit unallocated payment segment earns no interest

_Required Behavior:_

Interest calculated on bill segment balances AND credit unallocated payment segments, thus €20 credit unallocated payment segment earns monthly interest in favor of taxpayer

 

*Example Business Cases resulting in Unallocated Payment Segments*
 # Payment Suspense Scenarios, where for example invalid reference number results to a payment that cannot be allocated to a specific party role.
 # Payment File Processing Errors during automated payment file processing due to for example corrupted payment data or reference number mismatch.
 # Insufficient liability balance for full allocation as per the business example above. 
 # Payment Event State Transitions, when for example re-opening completed payment events where original segments need to be cancelled or payment event re-distribution scenarios requiring segment reallocation. 

*Documentation*
Document all the above adjustments for penalty and interest rule "CREDIT_INT". 

 

*Non functional requirements*
Performance , Security, Traceability, Accessibility, Usability  DODs should be fulfilled.
Feature | IRM-38238 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | PERFORMANCE EFFICIENCY | Green coding CI/CD flow optimization | Other | PI28 | 20.8 | p3 | To Do | {panel:title=Task}
To improve the platform maturity index, resource utilization must be optimized with a focus on Green Coding principles. To achieve this, existing CI/CD processes should be reviewed, adjusted, and ultimately optimized. Current documentation must also be updated to reflect these changes to the CI/CD workflows.
{panel}
{panel:title=Current state}
Jenkins is used to fully support CI/CD processes and flows.
{panel}
{panel:title=Solution}
*Review and Optimize Current Processes:*
 * *Reduce Build Frequency:* Adjust the process to reduce the number of builds executed by Jenkins. For example, ensure that Merge Requests in "Draft" state do not trigger builds.
 * *Optimize Caching:* Investigate using or optimizing cache strategies to boost the efficiency of Jenkins builds.
 * *Review Retention Policies:* Verify if cleaning policies are applied in the artifact repository (Nexus) for both Maven artifacts and Docker images{panel}

Feature | IRM-16272 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | PIT | PIT - File Original Personal Income Tax Return from Self Service – User | Other | PI30 | 130.9 | p3 | Under Analysis | As a self service user, I want to file an original personal income tax return for a specific filing period, so that I can meet my obligation to file a personal income tax return with correct data and on time as stipulated in the tax law.

*Introduction*

Personal income tax return that will be presented on the self service will have the same form sections and form fields as the example personal income tax return that has been described in IRM-14601.

Assumption is that the following self service requirements related to personal income tax are already supported:
 * User can login to the self service portal to deal with the tax matters for a specific party in a specific to which this user has been granted access
 * User can see what filing obligations exist for this party in a specific role for personal income tax and see the status of each of these obligations
 * User can see the personal income tax assessment for a specific filing / payment obligation
 * User can see what payment obligations exist for personal income tax assessments for which this specific party in a specific role is liable
 * User can see what payment obligations exist for any additional charges that have been levied towards a personal tax assessment (e.g. late payment interest) and for which this party in a specific role is considered liable
 * User can pay a liability that exists for a personal income tax assessment and any related charges for this party in a specific role
 * User can see the balance for personal income tax for this party in a specific role

Following self service requirements related to the personal income tax have not been implemented yet and are not in scope of this feature.
 * User can see that income that was paid by employers to this party in a specific role, and that the taxes and social contributions that were already deducted by these employers, are prefilled in the income form section of a pending personal income tax return
 * User can save a draft of a pending personal income tax return, and can open and complete a draft personal income tax return at a later point in time
 * User can see a notification that the personal income tax has been assessed for the filing period for which the personal income tax return was submitted

*Functional Requirements*
 * User can create a pending original personal income tax return for a filing period for which no original personal income tax has been submitted yet. User can see the form sections for taxpayer details, bank account details, income details, details on deductions, cost of living details, final tax assessment and attachments, and the related form fields as described in IRM-14601. Any meta data related to a personal income tax return (e.g. form source, related risk observations and related bill segments) should not be shown on the self service.
 * User can see that the taxpayer details and bank account details are prefilled in a pending personal income tax return
 * User can fill in the necessary details in the bank account details, income details, details on deductions, cost of living details, final tax assessment and attachments form sections
 * User can submit the personal income tax return once completed
 * User can see if there are any validation exceptions that prevent the pending personal income tax return from being submitted. User can navigate from a validation exception to the related form section and form field(s) to resolve any issues.
 * User can open a submitted personal income tax return to see what data was included in that return

Feature | IRM-16273 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | PIT | PIT - Amend Original Personal Income Tax Return from Self Service – User | Other | PI30 | 130.9 | p3 | Under Analysis | As a self service user, I want to amend an already submitted original personal income tax return, so that changes in my income or deductions are reflected in the adjusted personal income tax return.

*Introduction*

This feature is related to IRM-1973 in which requirements have been documented to record adjustments to the data in an input form that was already posted and post any differences that result from these adjustments.

*Functional Requirements*
 * User can amend an original personal income tax return that was submitted and processed. User can only amend the personal income tax return for the current filing period or for the two prior filing periods. And a user can amend an original personal income tax return more than once. User cannot amend an original personal income tax return if the original personal income tax return has not been submitted or processed yet. If an original income tax return was already amended, then the user can only amend the income tax return again if the previously amended return has also been submitted and processed.

 * User can open a submitted amended personal income tax return to see what data was included in that return
 * Any updates to the personal income tax return input form, form rules and process that have been implemented in the Revenue Management application (see IRM-14601), that are required to support amended tax returns are also in scope of this feature. When processing an amended original personal income tax return in the Revenue Management application, the difference between the personal income tax assessment in this return and the assessment of the original personal income tax return or the latest submitted and processed personal income tax return that amended this original personal income tax return should be posted.

Feature | IRM-38250 | CORE SUPPORTING CAPABILITIES | REFERENCE DATA | Enhance codelist items codes flexibility and historical track in Solon Tax | GRC | PI28 | 522.9 | p1 | In Design | As an RM Admin, I can update reference data with a codelist item having a code that is not unique, while its description is updated with different validity periods (no overlap), so as to comply with EU regulating updates.

*Introduction* 

*Tax Activity Codes in the EU:* There is no single "tax code" for all EU members. Instead, three main systems are used:
 * {*}NACE Codes{*}: The official statistical classification for economic activities. The current version is *NACE Rev. 2.1* (effective Jan 1, 2025). Attached in this feature for reference. 
 * {*}VAT Category Codes{*}: Standardized letters (e.g., *S* for Standard, *E* for Exempt) used in electronic invoicing.
 * {*}VATEX Codes{*}: Specific codes used to justify *VAT exemptions* based on EU Directive 2006/112/EC.
 * *Customs Codes (TARIC/CN)* For the import/export of goods, the Combined Nomenclature (CN) is used, which is an 8-digit coding system. 

In Greece, AADE (Independent Authority for Public Revenue) has proceeded with the mapping of the old activity codes (KAD 2008) to the new KAD 2025, a process which began on March 1, 2026. There is a direct correlation between Greek KAD (Activity Code Numbers) and NACE codes. KAD constitute the national version of the European NACE classification.
 * {*}Structure{*}: The first 4 characters of an eight-digit Greek KAD are fully identical to the 4 characters of the corresponding NACE code.
 * {*}2026 Harmonization{*}: AADE recently proceeded (as of 01/03/2026) with an automatic update of KADs for 1.9 million Tax IDs (AFM), in order to fully harmonize them with the new European standard {*}NACE Rev. 2.1{*}.
 * {*}Purpose{*}: This mapping ensures that economic activities in Greece are comparable to those of other EU member states for statistical and regulatory purposes.

*When a Code is Updated*

When the EU updates the NACE structure:
 * {*}Automatic Migration{*}: Most codes are automatically updated by national tax authorities (like AADE in Greece) if there is a 1-to-1 match.
 * {*}Manual Selection{*}: If one old code splits into multiple new ones, the taxpayer must manually select the most accurate one via the tax portal.
 * {*}Description Changes{*}: A code's number *can stay the same while its description* *is updated* to reflect modern technology or clearer definitions.

Validity and History
 * {*}Historical Accuracy{*}: A code must be valid for the period it was used. If you are filing an amended return for 2024, you use the code that was active in 2024, not the new 2025/2026 version.
 * {*}EU-Wide Validity{*}: This principle of historicity applies to all EU countries. While the digital portals differ (e.g., myAADE in Greece), the transition logic to NACE Rev. 2.1 is harmonized across the Union.

For Greek Tax Authority
The code *must remain valid* for the period prior to the change, as tax and statistical representation follows the principle of historicity. In practice, this means the following: * {*}Principle of Historicity{*}: For any transaction, declaration, or audit concerning the past (e.g., fiscal year 2024), the code that was in effect *at that time* is used. New codes (e.g., KAD 2025/2026) apply only to actions from their effective date onwards.
 * {*}System Maintenance{*}: AADE and Eurostat systems maintain the "historical versions" of the codes. If you need to file an amended return for a previous year, you must use the old code that corresponded to that specific period.
 * {*}Migration (Mapping){*}: The mapping performed by AADE does not "erase" the past; it creates a new entry in your Registry history. The "Registry Certificate" will show the expiration date of the old code and the start date of the new one.
 * {*}Audits and Cross-checks{*}: In the event of a tax audit for a past fiscal year, auditors examine the activity based on the description and the code that were in effect at the time of the transaction.

The current Solon Tax platform implementation requires unique codes for codelist items within the same codelist. However, EU tax regulations, particularly for tax activity codes (NACE, VAT Category, VATEX), require the ability to maintain the same code with different descriptions across different validity periods to support historical accuracy and regulatory compliance.

*Current Implementation Support*

The platform currently supports:
 * Unique code constraint for codelist items within a codelist
 * Basic validity period management with valid_from and valid_to fields
 * Codelist item labels with language support

*To Be Implementation*

Allow the same code to be added for different validity periods with:
 * No overlap between validity periods for the same code
 * Different descriptions for the same code across different time periods
 * Historical data preservation for reporting and backdated updates

*Functional Business Requirements*
 # {*}Historical Code Management{*}: Enable codelist items to have the same code with different descriptions across non-overlapping validity periods
 # {*}Temporal Data Integrity{*}: Ensure no validity period overlaps exist for items with the same code within a codelist
 # {*}Backdated Processing Support{*}: Allow selection of historical codelist items when processing backdated taxpayer updates
 # {*}Regulatory Compliance{*}: Support EU tax code evolution requirements (NACE Rev. 2.1)
 # {*}Reporting Continuity{*}: Maintain historical reference data for accurate reporting across different time periods

*Documentation*
Document all the above adjustments for updating reference data to support compliance with EU updates codes not unique per validity period.

 

*Non functional requirements*
Performance , Security, Traceability, Accessibility, Usability  DODs should be fulfilled.

Feature | IRM-37212 | CORE REVENUE MANAGEMENT CAPABILITIES | REGISTRATION | View Organizational structure and taxpayers hierarchy structure – User / Part 2 of 2 | GRC | PI28 | 746.9 | p1 | In Design | cont. [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-11539] 
As a revenue official, I want to view a graphical representation of the organizational structure, so that I can see what organizational units are part of the organizational structure and see how these organizational units are related to one another.

Similarly for party to party hierarchy, I need to be able to see similar representation. 
a) Org units : Revenue department itself is structured (e.g., Head Office -> Regional Office -> Local Branch).
b) Taxpayers:  relationships between legal entities, such as a Holding Company and its subsidiaries, or a franchisor and franchisees or main brand with branches -WHEN THESE FOR A BUSINESS REASON are not expressed in the system as party roles (that is recommended) 

Dependency:  IRM-36002 

 

*SCOPE : List view, searching and party assignment.* 

*Functional Requirements*

+Organizational Units+
 * In Org Units page: User can click a button to see an org. units tree where each node in this tree represents an descendant Org. Unit For each node the user can see information that uniquely identifies an Org. Unit. 
 * Within the tree the user can select to open an organizational unit to see more details in a new page.
 * In list page: User may click the Parent Org. unit link to open the parent Org unit. 
 * Users can search for the immediate parent or any ancestor organizational unit.

+Organizations / Taxpayers (Parties)+
 * In Party page history view, the user may assign a parent party.
 * In Party page as today view it displays a link of the parent Party (if any), which if selected opens the parent Party page.
 * In list page: User may see any parent party as link. User may click the link to open the parent party in a new page. 
 * Users can search for the immediate parent or any ancestor party.

+Assets+
 * In Asset page: User can click a button see an Asset tree where each node in the tree represents an descendant Asset. For each entity the user can see information that uniquely identifies this Asset.
 * Within the descendants' tree representation a user can click any node to see more details in a new page.
 * In Assets page history view, the user may assign a parent asset.
 * In Assets page as today view it displays a link of the parent asset (if any), which if selected opens the parent Party page.
 * In list page: User may see any parent Assets as link. User may click the link to open the parent Asset. 
 * In Asset page: User can click a button to see an tree representation where each node in the tree represents an descendant Asset. For each Asset the user can see information that uniquely identifies an Asset.
 * In this tree a user can open in a new page any descendant Asset to see more details.
 * Users can search for the immediate parent or any ancestor asset.

-+Example :+- 
-A button available in Level 1 Taxpayer  "Show Hierarchy"- 
-When click a modal with tree format appears:- 

-Level 1 Taxpayer A (Business account/ Brand HQs  & Accounting unit)-

            -Level 2 TaxpayerA1 (branch)-

Feature | IRM-37845 | CORE REVENUE MANAGEMENT CAPABILITIES | REGISTRATION | Enhance Validity period conditions in Registry detail entities to support multiple modifications in the same date | GRC | PI28 | 746.9 | p1 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As a revenue officer I need to be able to complete several Party details changes in the same date and system will allow this without effecting uniqueness and overlapping checks that are applied to Party and Party Role child entities with valid-from/valid-to periods.

The same logic must also apply when system determines which registry records are considered valid for a specific date (e.g., Today view in the UI or a historical date view).

The solution should be able to support same day changes for : 

a) records with valid-from/valid-to dates are considered duplicated or overlapping.
b) primary records with valid-from/valid-to dates are considered duplicated.
c) The criteria used to determine which records are valid on a specific reference date (current date or historical date).

Child objects to be considered : 
 * {color:#172b4d}Party role{color}
 * {color:#172b4d}party_identifier, party_name{color}
 * Party_state, party_address, party_contact ,Bank account  , Preferences,  party_classification, party additional details
 * {color:#172b4d}party_role_relationship, asset_party_role_relationship, asset_to_asset_relationship, valuation , party role eligible states {color}

Assumption : We assume that the error handing and the exceptions logged as well as the remaining uniqueness validations mechanisms are functional in the product for all registry entities. (Party , Party role, Claimant, User, Organ. Unit, Asset)

 

*Functional requirements*

 

*New Fields* 

For all the above mentioned Party child objects, Party , Party Role, add Optional fields
 * *Valid State?* , Boolean 
Default value = true
 * *Valid State  Reason*
Free text 
 * (!)   Define if a record type should be checked for uniqueness or not. This may create conflicts that there are suggested rules to overcome. 
*Field: Check if unique?*  /Boolean
Default value = true
Suggestion add this configuration in Code list items as metadata for party child objects types.  (e.g.,  Name type, ID type)
 * Make fields searchable
 * Make fields visible in the UI
 * Make fields updatable as/where the Valid from /to fields are
 * Move the information to relevant Party role sections (as Valid from/to) 
 * Default values :
 ** All existing records are migrated with valid_state = true
 ** All existing records are migrated with Check if unique= true

*Rules for Unique record check:*

For the same record type (or per case additional filters are used, such as in Identifiers the country) , 
If the record is *flagged as Valid*
check  if the period is not overlapping other periods if *CheckifUnique* is checked as true. If checked as false then no need to make any checks for the specific record or include this record in other checks.  In case of conflicts the first option based on start date sorting,  that is valid = true will be selected. 
In case of *end date = other records start date* then the end date overlapping with other record start date is ignored. (i.e. only end date of one period is the same as the start date of another period, see bullet 4) 
Start date is checked primary to define the period that record is valid. 

 

+Basics:+ 
 # If a record  flag {*}Valid{*}? = false : it is ignored during uniqueness checks and for primary checks.
 # If a record  flag {*}CheckifUnique{*}? = false : it is ignored during uniqueness checks and for primary checks.  Record can be valid.  (!)

+Examples Conditions:+

1 . If a record *Start date* = {*}End date{*}= *Y*  , Flag Valid ? = true  :
record is selected primary or considered *proper* entry for date Y   (primary set for start date Y,  if flagged as primary) 

2.  If  Record 1 start date end = A  and end date = X  , valid = true
and Record 2 start date = X , end date = B , valid = true
Then these records are not considered overlapping (although in current rule are consider overlapping). This is a *proper* condition. 
On date X, the valid record is Record2 (the record with start date X)
Not the one with end date = X (Record 1).

3.  If Record1: start date is null , end date  = X  , valid = true
Record2: start date  = X , end date  = null  , valid = true
The record 2 is selected primary or the considered for date x . This is a *proper* condition. 

3.  If Record1: start date is null , end date  = null  , valid = true
Record2: start date  = X , end date  = null   , valid = true
 System will not allow this because of overlapping in other days because of start dates(!)

4. If two records of the same type, 
and both have Valid state = true, 
when their validity periods overlap as they have same start date the system rejects the change due to overlapping validity periods. (!)
Record1: start date  =  X, end date  = A  , valid = true
Record2: start date  =  X , end date  = B  , valid = true

If  ** CheckifUnique? = false  , and we need to identity the value applicable per period, we will use the start date ignoring the end date overlap. 

+Other :+
 # A record is considered for date D when: 
valid state = true and 
start date <= D AND (end date is null OR end date > D)
or
If start date = end date = D
 # If multiple changes occur in the same transaction, Uniqueness validation must run after the end of batch updates. 
 # If valid_state = false , state_reason must be populated
 # If all record for a type are not valid then the system will behave like not having any record available
 # (as mentioned above) . If Check if Valid id checked as false then no need to make any checks for the specific record or include this record in other checks.  In case of conflicts the first option based on start date sorting,  that is valid = true will be selected.
 # If valid to = null means infinite validity
 # API queries using reference dates follow the same validity rules
 # the  included fields in uniqueness checks already considered (e.g. in Identities the countries, or the type of the record) should continue be used.

 

*Apply to :*
 * Validation of Uniqueness of primary records per period
 * Validation of Uniqueness of records per type (and other flags as per entity) per period
 * Define the visibly records that defines the view of today, history date, date in the past 

*UI :*

BE able to  Filter history records by valid from date
 If valid_state = false , state_reason must be populated
Project may define if  Valid = false and Check if unique is false records should be displayed or not.

15/1 -> Anna Papa

Document all the above adjustments. 

 

*Non functional requirements*
Performance , Security, Accessibility, Usability  DODs should be fulfilled.

Feature | IRM-30360 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | SECURITY | Data visibility permissions / Row level access, per hierarchical level of users in teams | GRC | PI29 | 1232 | p1 | To Do | As an admin I need to reassure that permissions of some of the system records are assigned hierarchical. 

In system Organizational Hierarchy will be implemented via Organizational Units, where a permission level role is assigned. 

The row level security will initially define the restrictions on records visibility. The hierarchical permissions will now grant permissions when restricted by row level. 

*Introduction*

The hierarchy is expected to be implemented introducing in higher levels leaders that to get leader permissions should be flagged as "Task Assigner " (It is permitted to add members but permissions should  be defined) 
Higher levels may have visibility permissions to records of the defined types  of the lower records of the same branch. Will not have access to the other branched unless records are publicly visible. 

Note that some of the below permissions, can be achieved by OPA rules in row level security.  
!image-2025-10-09-19-58-53-208.png|width=292,height=349!

 

 

*Functional Requirements*

While adding users under Organization units,  the permissions managed in hierarchy level should be defined. 
 * *Entity/Record types  to be affected Hierarchically by Org Units :*
 ** Time off requests : Permissions on CRUD, Assignments, Approvals based on user's Organization for Time Off requests
 ** Human Task (Assignments ):  Permission to Assign 
 ** Cases (Assignments ):  Permission to Assign 
 ** Users (Visibility)  : visibility of details 
 ** Resource Calendars : Permissions to see assigned calendar details 

 * *Default Visibility & Ownerships*
Owner/Mine  : I am assigner or the user that represents this record
Manager: I am in higher hierarchy "IS HEAD"
 ** The above users (owner, manager) gain by default read access to records.
 ** i.e. per entity: 
Human Tasks, Cases :  a) Assigned to Human task or b) if unassigned , eligible user or manager of eligible user
User : User + Manager
Resource Calendars : Assigned user  + Manager
Time off requests : Requestor /User  + Manager
 ** The users not assigned to any category does not have visibility to records. 

 * *Sharing Assignments Permissions per Hierarchy levels per Organizational Level* **
 ** Lower level same branch -> permissions  for the users assigned below in hierarchy
 ** Same level same branch  -> permissions  for the users assigned in same level of hierarchy
 ** Higher level same branch or top level -> permissions  for the users assigned higher in hierarchy
 ** Same level Different branch
 ** Higher level Different branch or top level
 ** Lower level Different branch 
 ** Mine - see above
 ** Admin : a special permission to see and modify all
 ** Permissions may be combined if user is assigned to several org units 
 * *Permissions* 
 ** *Read* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)  /  *DEFAULT PERMISSIONS when IS HEAD*
 ** *Assign* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)
 ** *Approve* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)
 ** *Edit* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)
 ** *Cancel* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)
 ** *Delegate Tasks* Entity type records , Select Record type (e.g. Time Off requests)

if the categories are like that and should be combined in a matrix

Feature | IRM-38847 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | SECURITY | Data Security - Restrict Access to Personal Data GDPR- Admin (based on data classifications) - Encrypt/decrypt -  Part 4/4 | Other | PI29 | 395.5 | p3 | To Do | cont, [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-20329] 
depends on https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-20328 

As an admin, I want to restrict access to sensitive personal data, so that only users that have a legitimate reason to access this data are granted access and unauthorized access to this data is prevented.

*Introduction*

This feature is related to the epic IRM-3106 in which requirements have been documented to secure the information in the revenue management system from unauthorized access.

This feature is related to IRM-30322 in which requirements have been documented to classify fields (or characteristics or categories of attachments) in the application as fields that contain non-personal, personal or sensitive personal data GDPR. However, not each field that has been classified to contain (sensitive) personal data will always contain personal data, as these fields (e.g. identifier or address fields) may also be used to record data for parties that are not natural persons. Only if the data in these fields is related to a natural person (see IRM-20315), it can be considered personal data. Exception to this rule is data that cannot be related to or has not yet been related to a specific party, such as data in forms, uploaded payment data or messages in the message store that cannot or not yet be related to a specific party. This data should be considered personal if the data has been classified as such.

*Functional Requirements*
 * Admin can choose to show or hide encrypted personal data on the user interface for users that do not have access to the decrypted sensitive personal data
 * Admin can define that decrypted personal data is shown on the user interface for users that do have access to the decrypted sensitive personal data
 * {color:#172b4d}Admin should be able to encrypt personal data details from logs (audit)/exception/message store , data areas, notes, forms, cases/ human task comments.{color}

 

*Documentation*
Document all the above adjustments. 

 

*Non functional requirements*
It is expected to reassure that relevant NFRs (Performance , Security, Accessibility, Usability ) are tested and are not negatively affecting the product.  
DODs should be fulfilled.
Feature | IRM-33406 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | MAINTAINABILITY | Integrate Self-Contained Documentation Portal into Solon Tax Deliverable | Other | PI28 | 48 | p3 | To Do | As a Solon Tax user on a customer-hosted environment, I want to access relevant help documentation directly from the Solon Tax hosted environment, so that I can get assistance without needing seperate access to connect to {{[https://docs.netcompany.com/]}} site

*Description:*

Currently, the Solon Tax UI integrates with the internal documentation portal at {{{}[https://docs.netcompany.com/]{}}}. This setup is not desired for customer-premise deployments which are often in isolated environments.

This story covers the work required to package, deploy, and integrate a self-contained version of the Solon Tax documentation portal within the standard Solon Tax product deliverables.

*Acceptance Criteria:*
 # A new process exists to build a stripped-down Docker image of the documentation portal, containing only the Solon Tax documentation.
 # A new Helm chart is created to deploy this documentation Docker image as part of the standard Solon Tax vanilla deployment.
 # The Solon Tax UI is reconfigured to retrieve help pages from the newly deployed, in-cluster documentation service instead of the external {{{}docs.netcompany.com{}}}.
 # Access to the bundled documentation site is secured; users must be authenticated and authorized through the existing Solon Tax access control mechanisms.
 # Unauthenticated users are prevented from accessing the documentation content.
 # Documentation on installation deliverables, installation procedure and architecture are updated accordingly.

Feature | IRM-30741 | NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENT COVERAGE | MAINTAINABILITY | Introduce ArchUnit | Other | PI28 | 373.1 | p1 | In Design | *Problem Statement*

As the SolonTax codebase grows in size and complexity, it becomes increasingly difficult to manually enforce architectural guidelines and design principles ( see D0160 Programming Guidelines) during code reviews. This leads to several risks:
 * *Architectural Drift:* Over time, the code can deviate from its intended design (e.g., layered architecture, domain model purity), leading to tight coupling and reduced maintainability.
 * *Inconsistent Code Reviews:* Architectural violations can be easily missed during manual reviews, as reviewers are often focused on business logic.
 * *Increased Technical Debt:* Unchecked violations accumulate as technical debt, making future development, refactoring, and onboarding of new team members more difficult and costly.

There is currently no automated mechanism to prevent such architectural decay, making the system's long-term health dependent on tribal knowledge and manual vigilance.

*Proposed Solution*

This enabler will introduce {*}ArchUnit{*}, a free Java library for checking the architecture of your code, into our build and test lifecycle. By writing plain Java unit tests, we can codify our architectural rules and automatically verify them.

The solution involves:
 # *Integrating ArchUnit:* Add the ArchUnit dependency to the project's build configuration (e.g., Maven or Gradle).
 # *Creating an Architecture Test Suite:* Establish a dedicated test source set or package for architectural tests.
 # *Implementing Foundational Rules:* Implement an initial set of high-value architectural rules to serve as a baseline and a template for future rules. These tests will run as part of the standard CI/CD pipeline, failing the build if a violation is detected.

This will provide immediate, automated feedback to developers and act as a powerful "guardrail" to prevent architectural erosion.

*Acceptance Criteria*
 # *Dependency Integration:* The ArchUnit library is successfully added as a test-scoped dependency.
 # *Test Suite Creation:* A dedicated maven module is created to house all ArchUnit tests.
 # *CI/CD Integration:* The architectural test suite is configured to run automatically as part of the continuous integration pipeline during unit tests phase. A build must fail if any architectural rule is violated.
 # *Baseline Pass:* All newly introduced architectural tests pass against the existing codebase on the main development branch. If any pre-existing violations are found, they must be either fixed or explicitly exempted as part of this task's scope.

*Out of Scope*
 * This enabler focuses on establishing the framework and implementing a foundational set of rules. Defining an exhaustive list of every possible architectural rule is not in scope.
 * Large-scale refactoring of the existing codebase to fix numerous pre-existing violations is out of scope, unless a small, agreed-upon number of fixes are required to establish a clean baseline.

Feature | IRM-16516 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | SELF SERVICE ACCOUNT OVERVIEW | SS  Payments - See Taxpayer Account Overview - User - Part 3 - Open/Edit Registration Details | Other | PI29 | 74.9 | p3 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As a self service user, I want to see an overview of a taxpayer account that I can access, so that I can confirm this is the taxpayer account that I intended to access, can understand the obligations for this account, can see notifications sent to this account and see the taxpayer account balances.

*Introduction*

This feature is related to IRM-3447 in which requirements have been doccumented to see an overview of a taxpayer account on the self service.

Some example wireframes have been attached to this feature.  In case the content on the wireframes differs from the functional requirements, then the functional requirement should be used as input when implementing this feature.

*Functional requirements*
 * User can see registration details of the taxpayer.
 ** {color:#c1c7d0}Data set:{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Name: the primary name of the taxpayer for which the account overview is shown{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}ID type: the type of the primary identifier of the taxpayer for which the account overview is shown{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}ID number: the primary identifier number of the taxpayer for which the account overview is shown{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Address: the preferred address for communication with the taxpayer for which the account overview is shown{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Email: the preferred email address for communication with the taxpayer for which the account overview is shown{color}
 ** Actions:
 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open the registration details{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open and update the registration details{color}
 * {color:#c1c7d0}User can see the current balances for each tax type for which this taxpayer was registered{color}
 ** {color:#c1c7d0}Data set - can contain data for multiple tax types{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Tax type: a tax type for which this taxpayer was registered{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Balance: the current balance for a tax type for which a taxpayer was registered - any period in which the tax type was applicable for this taxpayer should be considered when calculating the balance{color}
 ** {color:#c1c7d0}Actions:{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}User can open the details for a specific tax type for which this taxpayer was registered (see IRM-3449){color}
 * {color:#c1c7d0}User can see the past, present, and future obligations and their status for the taxpayer account in a timeline{color}
 ** {color:#c1c7d0}Data set - can contain data for multiple obligations{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Tax type: the tax type for which the obligation exists{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Obligation action type: the type of action that the taxpayer is obliged to take{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Period: the period for which the obligation exists (if any){color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Status: the status of the action that the taxpayer is obliged to take - user can for example see if the action has been completed or not - and see for actions that have not been completed yet whether the action is considered overdue or not (e.g. overdue is red, due is orange and completed is green){color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Obligation Due date: the date by which the action, that the taxpayer is obliged to take, must be completed{color}
 ** {color:#c1c7d0}Actions:{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}User can open the details for a specific obligation{color} (see IRM-3451)
 * {color:#c1c7d0}User can see the latest notifications{color}
 ** {color:#c1c7d0}Data set - can contain data for multiple notifications{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Notification date: the date the notification was sent to the taxpayer{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Notification message: the notification message header{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Notification read or unread: indication whether the user has read the message ate least once or not{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}Notification importance: the importance of the notification{color}
 ** {color:#c1c7d0}Actions:{color}
 *** {color:#c1c7d0}User can open the details for a specific notification{color}
