Feature | IRM-5111 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | SELF SERVICE FILING & PAYMENTS | SS Payments - See Filing Obligation Details - Part 2 | Other | PI29 | 392 | p3 | To Do | As a self service user, I want to see the details of a specific filing obligation for a specific taxpayer, so that I can see what forms have been created and/or already filed as a result of this obligation, what amounts have been assessed as a result of filing these forms, and what other information has been exchanged with the revenue authority related to this filing obligation such as supporting documents and notices.

*Introduction*

Some example wireframes have been attached to this feature. In case the content on the wireframes differs from the functional requirements, then the functional requirement should be used as input when implementing this feature.

*Functional Requirements*
 * User can see the details of a specific filing obligation for a specific taxpayer

 ** Actions:

 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open a new or draft amended tax return form for a filing obligation. Assumption is that the correct tax return form is opened for the specific tax type for which the overview is provided. Also, the assumption is that the tax return form can be prefilled with data that is already known - for example the taxpayer details, filing period details and data from the original tax return. User can only open a new or draft amended tax return if an original tax return has been submitted for this filing obligation. Assumption is that the user can only amend a tax return for specific tax types (e.g. for corporate income tax).{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open a payment form (see IRM-3542 for an example of a payment form) to pay the sum of all current positive balances of any payment obligations that are related to a specific filing obligation (e.g. late filing penalty or tax assessment and any related charges that were added after filing a tax return for this filing obligation). Assumption is that the payment form can be prefilled with data that is already known - for example the taxpayer details and the payment obligation details. User can only open a payment form if there is an outstanding amount that needs to be paid for these payment obligations.{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open a form to request a refund if an overpayment exists for one or more payment obligations that are related to a specific filing obligation (e.g. late filing penalty or tax assessment and any related charges that were added after filing a tax return for this filing obligation). Assumption is that the refund request form can be prefilled with data that is already known - for example the taxpayer details and the details of the payment obligations for which an overpayment exists. User can only open a refund request form if an overpayment amount exists for any of the payment obligations.{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open a form to request to offset an overpayment that exists for one or more payment obligations that are related to a specific filing obligation (e.g. late filing penalty or tax assessment and any related charges that were added after filing a tax return for this filing obligation). Assumption is that the request overpayment offset form can be prefilled with data that is already known - for example the taxpayer details and the overpayment amount that can be offset.{color}

 *** {color:#c1c7d0}User can upload a supporting document that can be used by the revenue authority to validate the content of the submitted tax return. User can only upload a document if the obligation to file a tax return has been met.
 *** User can open a financial overview (see IRM-3452) for the payment obligations that are related to a specific filing obligation (e.g. late filing penalty or tax assessment and any related charges that were added after filing a tax return for this filing obligation).
 * User can see what amounts have been assessed related to a specific filing obligation (e.g. late filing penalty or tax assessment that was added after filing a tax return for this filing obligation). Any charges (e.g. late payment penalty or interest) that are levied towards these original assessments are not considered in this overview.
 ** Data set - can contain data for multiple assessments
 *** Filing type: the type of submission that was done (e.g. submit preliminary, original or amended tax return)
 *** Letter reference number: unique reference number of the assessment notice in which the taxpayer was informed about the assessment
 *** Assessed amount: the amount that was assessed{color}

 
 * {color:#172b4d}User can see what draft tax returns exist for a specific filing obligation. These tax returns have not been submitted yet.{color}
 ** {color:#172b4d}Data set - can contain data for multiple draft tax returns - most often just one draft form{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Form type: the type of form that was saved as a draft{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Form reference number: the reference number of the form that was saved as a draft{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Last updated date: the date the draft form was last updated{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Status: the status of the form that was saved as a draft (e.g. saved){color}
 ** {color:#172b4d}Actions:{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open the draft tax return (see IRM-3539 for an example of a value added tax return form){color}
 * {color:#172b4d}User can see what supporting documents have been uploaded for a specific filing obligation.{color}
 ** {color:#172b4d}Data set - can contain data for multiple supporting documents{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Document type: the type of supporting document that was submitted to the revenue authority{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Document reference number: a unique reference number of the supporting document that was submitted to the revenue authority{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Submission date: the date the supporting document was submitted to the revenue authority{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Status: the status of submitting a supporting document (e.g. submitted){color}
 ** {color:#172b4d}Actions:{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open a supporting document{color}
 * {color:#172b4d}User can see what letters (e.g. reminder letter, notice letter) were sent to the taxpayer by the revenue authority.{color}
 ** {color:#172b4d}Data set:{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Letter type: the type of letter that was sent to the taxpayer{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Letter reference number: a unique reference for the letter that was sent to the taxpayer{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Description: a description of the letter that was sent to the taxpayer{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}Letter date: the date the letter was considered to have been delivered to the taxpayer{color}
 ** {color:#172b4d}Actions:{color}
 *** {color:#172b4d}User can open a letter (see attached wireframe){color}

Feature | IRM-25436 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | SELF SERVICE FILING & PAYMENTS | SS Enhancements - Refactor existing self service pages to work through services implementation - part 4 / Important | GRC | PI29 | 1045.1 | p1 | Under Analysis | As an admin, I want to define what services are provided on the portal (e.g. view account overview, view obligation overview, view CIT return, file CIT return, pay an obligation, or file an objection) and what portal resources (e.g. menu item, input form, page or action) and permissible operations are required for each of these services, so that a portal user can easily grant sub-users and/or representative users access to these services for the parties in specific roles to which this portal user has been linked or has been granted access to.

 

Specifically, it should include the security solution for submitting forms and making payments which were descoped from part 1 feature. Any other item required according to architecture decisions should be considered here.

When this is implemented the self service application should not user any pass through endponts towards the backend system 

 

Check linked stories for relevant work in this feature
Feature | IRM-25436 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | SELF SERVICE FILING & PAYMENTS | SS Enhancements - Refactor existing self service pages to work through services implementation - part 4 / Important | GRC | PI28 | 112 | p1 | Under Analysis | As an admin, I want to define what services are provided on the portal (e.g. view account overview, view obligation overview, view CIT return, file CIT return, pay an obligation, or file an objection) and what portal resources (e.g. menu item, input form, page or action) and permissible operations are required for each of these services, so that a portal user can easily grant sub-users and/or representative users access to these services for the parties in specific roles to which this portal user has been linked or has been granted access to.

 

Specifically, it should include the security solution for submitting forms and making payments which were descoped from part 1 feature. Any other item required according to architecture decisions should be considered here.

When this is implemented the self service application should not user any pass through endponts towards the backend system

Feature | IRM-3545 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | SELF SERVICE FILING & PAYMENTS | SS Payments - See Payment Details | Other | PI29 | 392 | p3 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As a self service user, I want to see the details of a specific payment, so that I can understand when and how the payment was made, understand what was paid and see the related payment receipt.

*Introduction*

Some example wireframes have been attached to this feature. In case the content on the wireframes differs from the functional requirements, then the functional requirement should be used as input when implementing this feature.

*Functional Requirements*
 * User can see the details of a specific payment
 ** Data set:
 *** Payment date: the date on which a payment was made by the user
 *** Payment method: the method that was used to make the payment
 *** Amount paid: the amount that was paid by the user
 *** Status: the status of the payment that was made by the user (e.g. accepted and cancelled)
 * User can see what payment form was submitted to make the payment
 * Data set
 ** Form type: the type of form that was submitted
 ** Form reference number: the reference number of the form that was submitted
 ** Submission date: the date the form was submitted
 ** Status: the status of the form that was submitted (e.g. submitted, being processed or processed)
 * Actions:
 ** User can open a submitted payment form (see IRM-3542 for an example of a payment form)


 * User can see the payment receipt that was provided after having completed the payment
 ** Data set:
 *** Receipt number: a unique reference for the payment receipt that was provided
 *** Creation date: the date the receipt was created
 ** Actions:
 *** User can open the receipt (see attached wireframe)
 * User can see what was paid with the payment.
 ** Data set:
 *** Tax type: description of the tax type to which the payment was distributed for the taxpayer
 *** Period: description of the period (if any) to which the payment was distributed for the taxpayer
 *** Amount paid: the amount that was paid to the specific tax type and period for the taxpayer

Feature | IRM-3542 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | SELF SERVICE FILING & PAYMENTS | SS  Payments - Submit Payment Form | Other | PI29 | 392 | p3 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As a self service user, I want fill in and submit a payment form to pay the amounts owed for certain payment obligations, so that I can meet these payment obligations towards the revenue authority.

*Introduction*

Some example wireframes have been attached to this feature. In case the content on the wireframes differs from the functional requirements, then the functional requirement should be used as input when implementing this feature.

*Functional Requirements*
 * User can see a payment form
 ** Data set:
 *** Taxpayer details
 **** Taxpayer name: name of the taxpayer for which the payment obligations exist - assumption is that the taxpayer name can be prefilled and is read-only
 **** Identification type: the primary identification type of the taxpayer - assumption is that the identification type can be prefilled and is read-only
 **** Identification number: the primary identification number of the taxpayer - assumption is that the identification type can be prefilled and is read-only
 *** Payment details
 **** Payment method: payment methods that the user can select from - payment method credit card is used as an example in this example
 **** Payment service provider: payment service providers that the user can select from - payment service provider can only be selected if there are multiple payment service providers that support the selected payment method
 **** Credit card: types of credit cards that the user can choose from
 **** Credit card number: number on the user's credit card
 **** Expiry date month: credit card will expire at the end of this month
 **** Expiry date year: credit card will expire in this year
 **** CVV Security Code: security code that can be found on the back of the credit card
 **** Name: name that is displayed on the front of the card
 *** Payment Obligations - can contain data of multiple payment obligations
 **** Tax type: description of the tax type for which the payment obligation exists - assumption is that this information is prefilled based on the payment obligations that were selected on a previous page (see for example IRM-3451 and IRM-3541) and read-only
 **** Period: description of the period (if any) for which the obligation to pay certain liabilities exist (e.g. late filing penalty or tax assessment and any related charges that were added after filing a tax return for this period) - assumption is that this information is prefilled based on the payment obligations that were selected on a previous page (see for example IRM-3451 and IRM-3541) and read-only
 **** Payable amount: the total outstanding amount for a payment obligation - assumption is that this information is prefilled based on the payment obligations that were selected on a previous page (see for example IRM-3451 and IRM-3541) and read-only
 **** Payment amount: amount that the user can enter to indicate how much should be paid for a specific payment obligation - assumption is that the payment amount is equal to the payable amount by default
 **** Total payable amount: the sum of the payable amounts of the selected payment obligations - assumption is that this amount is calculated and read-only
 **** Total payment amount: the sum of the amount that will be paid for the selected payment obligations - assumption is that this amount is calculated and read-only
 ** Actions:
 *** User can print a payment form as a PDF
 *** User can submit a payment form once the form has been filled in. User can see if there are any validation issues that need to be resolved before the value added tax return can be submitted. User can see a confirmation if the payment was successfully processed (see attached wireframe). User can open a payment receipt if the payment was successfully processed (see attached wireframe).

Feature | IRM-3541 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | SELF SERVICE FILING & PAYMENTS | SS  Payments - See Current Payment Obligations | Other | PI29 | 392 | p3 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As a self service user, I want to see what payment obligations exist for a specific taxpayer, so that I can take action to pay what is owed by the taxpayer to the revenue authority.

*Introduction*

Some example wireframes have been attached to this feature. In case the content on the wireframes differs from the functional requirements, then the functional requirement should be used as input when implementing this feature.

*Functional Requirements*
 * User can see the current payment obligations for a specific taxpayer
 ** Data set:
 *** Tax type: description of the tax type for which the obligation to pay certain liabilities exist
 *** Period: description of the period (if any) for which the obligation to pay certain liabilities exist (e.g. late filing penalty or tax assessment and any related charges that were added after filing a tax return for this period)
 *** Payable amount: the amount that the taxpayer is obliged to pay for the specific tax type in the specific period (if any)
 *** Status: the status of the payment action that the taxpayer is obliged to perform - user can see whether the action is considered overdue or not

 *** User can select one or more payment obligations for which the user wants to take action to pay what is owed to the revenue authority

Feature | IRM-374 | REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATIONS | SELF SERVICE FILING & PAYMENTS | SS Payments - Initiate Payment from Self Service Portal - User | GRC | PI29 | 507.5 | p2 | Under Analysis | As a taxpayer, I want to see and pay my outstanding liabilities from the self service portal, so that I can understand and meet my payment obligations towards the revenue authority.

*Introduction*

This feature describes how the taxpayer can use the taxpayer self service portal to initiate a payment to pay outstanding liabilities.

The steps the taxpayer must follow to initiate and complete a payment may vary depending on the type of integration between ICARUS and the payment service providers (a.k.a. payment gateways or PSPs). Integration types to consider are (1) hosted - taxpayer leaves self service portal to complete payment on PSP portal, (2) direct post - PSP page that is used to complete the payment is embedded in a frame on self service portal and (3) non-hosted - self service portal provides features to capture all payment details and uses an API to submit details to the PSP. This feature describes the requirements assuming the 3rd type of integration is used.

Revenue authorities can depending on the requirements provide various options on the self service portal to pay outstanding liabilities, including for example (1) pay party role, (2) pay specific tax account, (3) pay a specific filing period, (4) pay a specific pay plan, (5) pay a specific collection notice, (6) pay a specific tax return, or (7) pay a specific single assessed liability (e.g. tax, penalty or interest). This feature describes the requirements for the 3rd and 7th option.

Revenue authorities can depending on the requirements provide various payment methods on the self service portal to pay outstanding liabilities. Examples include (1) credit card, (2) debit card, (3) PayPal and other similar services, (4) M-Pesa, Paym and other similar services, (5) direct debit, (6) PDS2 and other similar services and (7) guarantees registered at the revenue authority. This feature describes the requirements for the 1st option.

Revenue authorities and/or payment service providers may charge convenience fees. Information on any applicable fees must be presented to the portal user before submitting the payment. Convenience fee requirements will be documented in another feature.

As credit card details are used in the self service portal, the product should cater for features to allow the revenue authority to be PCI-DSS compliant. Relevant PCI-DSS requirements will be documented in another feature.

*Functional requirements*
 * User can select outstanding liabilities for payment. Examples in scope for this feature are:
 ** User can see a list with outstanding liabilities. Examples of properties to display in the list are the debt category, revenue type, filing period, notice reference number, payable amount and status of the liability (e.g. pending or overdue). User can select one or more outstanding liabilities for payment. See example on attached screenshot 'ICARUS Self Service Pay Specific Assessed Liabilities Example.png'. Multi-select and passing data to another action will be implemented as part of IRM-401.
 ** User can see the assessed liabilities (including outstanding liabilities) for a specific filing period (on the filing obligation details page). User can choose to pay all outstanding liabilities for the filing period or choose to pay a single assessed liability. See example on attached screenshot 'ICARUS Self Service Pay Specific Filing Period Example.png'.
 * User can enter the following data in the sample payment form.
 See example of form in attached screenshot 'ICARUS Self Service Payment Form Credit Card Example.png'
 ** Taxpayer Details
 *** Taxpayer Name (prefilled and read-only)
 *** Identification Type (prefilled and read-only)
 *** Identification Number (prefilled and read-only)
 ** Payment Details
 *** Payment Method (configurable list)
 *** Payment Service Provider (configurable list)
 Payment Service Provider field is only shown if there are multiple Payment Service Providers defined that support the selected Payment Method
 *** Credit Card (configurable list)
 *** Credit Card Number
 *** Expiry Date - Month
 *** Expiry Date - Year
 *** CVV Security Code
 *** Name on Card
 ** Payment Obligations (multiple; prefilled based on selected outstanding liabilities)
 *** Debt Category (prefilled)
 *** Revenue Type (prefilled)
 *** Period (prefilled)
 *** Reference Number (prefilled)
 *** Payable Amount (prefilled)
 *** Payment Amount
 User can enter the payment amount for each row with outstanding liability details.
 *** Total Payable Amount (calculated)
 *** Total Payment Amount (calculated)
 * User can see currency symbol for amounts.
 * User can save a draft of the payment form.
 * User can print the payment form to PDF.
 * User can submit the payment form to the Payment Service Provider.
 * User can see a payment confirmation message if the payment was successfully processed after submission. Examples of data displayed on the payment confirmation are the payment status, payment date, payment amount and payment receipt number. See example on attached screenshot 'ICARUS Self Service Payment Confirmation.png'.
 * If the payment could not be processed after submission, the user can see the validation exceptions in the payment form. Examples of reasons why the payment could not be processed are invalid credit card number and credit card is expired. The user should be able to correct the data entered in the payment form or to abort the attempt to pay
 * User can open the payment receipt. Examples of data displayed on the payment receipt are taxpayer name, taxpayer identification type, taxpayer identification number, taxpayer address, payment method, payment date, payment amount, and information about what was paid (e.g. tax type and filing period) (will be handled by IRM-380)
 * User can print the payment receipt to PDF (will be handled by IRM-380)

 *Note* that the form described above refers to the case of paying transactions. A different form should be created for the case of paying an obligation (Pay button on upper part of "ICARUS Self Service Pay Specific Filing Period Example.png"

Feature | IRM-36660 | CORE SELF SERVICE CAPABILITIES | SELF SERVICE SERVICES MANAGEMENT | Attachments in Forms - Document Uploads enhancements before and after saving the form / RM & SS | GRC | PI28 | 739.2 | p1 | In Design | As a taxpayer or revenue authority user, I want to upload and manage required attachments while filling in a form (even before saving it), including during registration forms where the relevant party is not yet created, so that I can complete the submission process without unnecessary interruptions. 

*Background*
In as-is system the form should be saved in order to be able to upload documents.

*Functional Requirements*
 * Users (revenue officer or taxpayer) can upload attachments with permitted metadata while filling the form, before saving.

 * Users can view the list of uploaded attachments while filling the form (before saving).

 * Before and After saving, users can:
View attachments
Add new attachments
Remove attachments
Edit metadata
 * In RM , users can link attachments to additional system records (e.g., case file) while managing form attachments.

 * If attachment upload fails:
The user is clearly informed by a message that attachment was not successfully uploaded. 
Form saving/submission is not blocked.
Successfully uploaded files remain attached. (Orphan issue).  

 * Attachments modifications after saving are stored in audit log

 

*Documentation*
Document all the above adjustments. 

*Non functional requirements*
It is expected team to get aligned with respective teams and reassure that is not creating issues or the related NFRs will be tested :
Performance , Security, Accessibility, Usability 
DODs should be fulfilled.
Feature | IRM-36982 | OTHER ACTIVITIES | SUPPORT TO PDM | Support to PdM - Before Feature Creation (Current PI27) | Other | PI29 | 8 |  |  | 
Feature | IRM-39196 | OTHER ACTIVITIES | SUPPORT TO PDM | Support to PdM - Before Feature Creation (Current PI28) | Other | PI28 | 600 |  |  | 
Feature | IRM-38899 | CORE REVENUE MANAGEMENT CAPABILITIES | TAX ACCOUNTS | Support Tax Account Overview Page in the Single Taxpayer Overview | GTM | PI28 | 395.5 | p1 | In Design | As a revenue officer, I want to have an overview of the financial transactions for a revenue type registration that represents a tax account, so that I can see an aggregated, holistic and coherent representation of the financial data of the the tax account in a specificied reconciliation period. 

*Introduction*

This feature describes the functional business requirements for a new single taxpayer overview page within Solon Tax, named the "Tax Account Overview". This new feature will introduce a period-centric overview. It will aggregate and present all financial transactions (FTs) related to a selected _reconciliation period(s)_ for a given revenue type registration, providing an immediate, consolidated view of that period's financial status. 

The purpose of this page is to provide a consolidated view of all Financial Transactions (FTs) associated with a specific reconciliation period for a taxpayer's Tax Account.

Currently, while Solon Tax supports the concept of a Tax Account ({{{}Skattekonto{}}}) and links Financial Transactions to reconciliation periods, there is no dedicated user interface that presents this information in a single, easily accessible view. This feature will bridge that gap, improving visibility and efficiency for Revenue Authority users managing these accounts.

As a reference countries that "Tax Account" is most prevalent in Europe, particularly in Scandinavia and the Nordics, which are global leaders in e-government. 

Currently implementation exists for the "Single Taxpayer Overview" pages, often refered to as 360 View, where a "Taxpayer Financial Overview" exists and can be used as reference. Particularly the last accordion of this page referred as " Financial Details per Financial Transaction". This is a page where all financial transactions for all revenue types are displayed and not only Tax Account that is the scope of this feature. 

*Functional Requirements*
h4. Navigation

A new redirect link shall be introduced on the *Revenue Type Registration (RTR)* page.
 * This link shall only be visible for RTRs that are configured as a "Tax Account" (i.e., where the {{isTaxAccount}} flag on the associated Revenue Type is true).
 * The link will navigate the user to the new "Tax Account Overview" page, passing the context of the current RTR and the selected reconciliation period.
 * Assumption is that the existing link from the party role will continue to function as is with the additional view in scope of this feature for the Tax Account. 

h4. Page Content and Layout

The "Tax Account Overview" page will contain the following elements:
 * *Filters:* User should be able to filter the following information:

 * 
 ** Reconciliation Period Filter
 ** From: 01/01/2026 
 ** To: 31/01/2026 or To: 31/03/2026, meaning more than one reconciliation periods can be selected. 

 
 * *"Update P&I" Button:* User should be able to see and select the "Update P&I" button where he/she can enter the "RECALCULATEFROMDATE" to run Penalty & Interest. 

 * *Financial Transactions Table:* A table displaying all Financial Transactions linked to the selected reconciliation period for the given Tax Account. The table should be read-only and provide standard functionalities like sorting, pagination and Column Configurator. The table should start with an opening balance for the period selected and end with the closing balance. 

Opening Balance of a period should be equal to the closing balance of the previous period. Opening balance should be the running balance of all financial transactions prior to date from selected in the filters. 

Closing Balance of a period is the running balance and should be equal to the Opening of that period plus any financial transaction related to that period such as debts, payments (both allocated and unallocated), interests, write offs, refunds... 

Available Columns (data) for FTs should be:  
 * Creation Date
 * Effective Date (eg. Period Reference - Period the debt/payment refers to)
 * Accounting Date 
 * Origin 
 * FT ID
 * Revenue Type 
 * FT Type 
 * Posting Reason
 * Liability Balance 
 * Running Balance

Please refer to the attached example_updated for a comprehensive view of the Tax Account Overview page.
h3. Assumptions & Dependencies
 * The Revenue Type entity has a configurable attribute to designate it as a "Tax Account."
 * The Financial Transaction entity has an attribute ({{{}reconciliationPeriodCode{}}}) to link it to a specific Reconciliation Period.

*Key features highlighted in this view:*
 * *Opening Balance:* The view starts with the "Opening Balance" showing the tax account's debt from before the selected period.
 * *Running Balance:* A column shows the balance after every single transaction, which is crucial for analysis.
 * *Detailed Descriptions:* Transactions are clearly labeled (e.g., "Payroll Tax Assessment," "Payment Received").
 * *Period Reference:* A column links a transaction back to the original tax period it relates to (e.g., Q4-2025), which is vital for an officer's investigation.

DODs should be fulfilled.

More over related to performance the team is expected to provide a solution on how the opening balance will be retrieved considering all past debts. Note that past debts may be related to periods, that may differ per revenue authority, for the last 10 years for example.

Feature | IRM-38308 | CORE REVENUE MANAGEMENT CAPABILITIES | TAX ACCOUNTS | Introduce a Threshold Amount Field in Revenue Type Registration to support Tax Account | GTM | PI29 | 507.5 | p1 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As a revenue officer I should be able to define a threshold amount for a revenue type registration so that the system can support Tax Account implementation. 

*Introduction* 

This analysis outlines the requirements for introducing a threshold amount field in the Revenue Type Registration entity to support Tax Account functionality in Solon Tax. The threshold field will enable implementation teams to configure automatic threshold determination rules while maintaining manual editability during the initial implementation phase. 

The threshold amount will be used in Tax Account scenarios where specific monetary limits determine processing behavior, validation rules, or reporting requirements. This field provides the foundation for threshold-based business logic while allowing implementation teams flexibility in defining automatic calculation rules.

*Functional Business Requirements*

Add a new field thresholdAmount to the Revenue Type Registration entity that:

> Stores a monetary threshold value for tax account processing
> Supports decimal precision for accurate financial calculations
> Allows null values (optional field)
> Is editable by users during creation and updates
> Can be automatically populated by system rules (future enhancement)



This enhancement provides the foundational threshold capability required for Tax Account implementations while maintaining the flexibility needed for diverse implementation requirements and future automatic rule integration.

*Documentation*
Document all the above adjustments for introducing a threshold amount filed in revenue type registration.

 

*Non functional requirements*
Performance , Security, Traceability, Accessibility, Usability  DODs should be fulfilled.

Feature | IRM-40159 | CORE REVENUE MANAGEMENT CAPABILITIES | TAXPAYER ACCOUNTING | Configurability of GL Decision Table - Be able to override by custom application | GRC | PI28 |  | p1 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As a configurator I need to be able to bypass using a custom solution the GL decision table mechanism. 

*Description* 
Notes from PSD: 

 _" Currently, the GL account decision logic is tightly integrated into the core Solon Tax product. This creates a constraint for projects with non-standard or complex GL posting requirements that cannot be satisfied by the default Drools-based decision mechanism._
 _-> Enable configurators to override the GL decision table mechanism with a custom adapter/application without modifying core product code._
_-> Projects need the ability to bypass the standard "getGLAccountCodeDecisions" mechanism and substitute it with their own custom implementation (adapter/application), similar to how the Allocation custom application works today._
_"_

*Functional Requirements*
 * Be able to bypass the "getGLAccontCodeDecisions" overriding it by a custom application/adapter.
 ** Move GL decision Code to Custom BE  as it is now the Allocation custom application.
 ** Important Note : The GL decision drools supported at that time by product  should be default in installation of the Solon. This will be the default unless projects need to configure it otherwise.

Feature | IRM-30362 | CORE REVENUE MANAGEMENT CAPABILITIES | TAXPAYER ACCOUNTING | GL decisions table - Ensure extensibility and high volume support of decisions /Functionality & Reference Implementation | GRC | PI29 | 1493.1 | p3 | Waiting Analysis Approval | As an administrator responsible for configuring the GL Decision Table (Accountant table), iI need to support the extensibility of the solution. 
I need to introduce additional parameters that control how GL accounts are split across multiple files or tables. This is required to support very high volumes of decision lines and complex business rules.
I need to allow custom adapters to be used on how rules are created and selected to generate journal entries. 

These parameters will allow the system to efficiently handle hundreds of special cases, reduce the size and complexity of individual GL decision tables, and improve maintainability by splitting configurations into multiple, logically grouped records. 

A realistic number of GL decision lines with the assumption that legacy GLs will be removed from time to time, is 200.000 lines

 

*Functional Requirements* 


+*1.* Some suggestions on how to support high volumes of rules:+ 

*A) GL Decision Line Volume Support*
 * Decision rule sheets must support modern XLSX row limits (1,048,576+ rows), not legacy XLS limits (65,536 rows).
 * The system should support the use of multiple decision lines per transaction (multi-lines), where applicable.

*B) Split GL Decision Tables Across Multiple Sheets or Files*
 * As an admin/configurator, I must be able to define and use more than one spreadsheet or files for GL Decision Tables.
 * Splitting must be rule-driven and configurable.

*C) Rule Evaluation Mechanism*

The system must determine which spreadsheet(s) to read based on configured split rules.
One FT may require reading:

A single sheet, or Multiple sheets, depending on customer-defined configuration.
Rule evaluation must be deterministic and transparent (traceable which sheets were evaluated).

 

*D)   Reference Implementation Split Strategies (Examples)*
 * The system should support splitting GL decision tables based on configurable parameters, such as FT Origin, RTR relation with Claimants etc: 
 ** Segment type of Origin  of Financial transactions (ft_origin_cl) , splitting spreadsheets for Bill segments, Payment segments, Allocation Segments. 
One sheet for Segment type = Bill segment, one for Payment Segments, one Allocation Segments
 ** If Claimant related (if the revenue type registration is related to a claimant) 
Use a dedicated spreadsheet containing claimant-specific GL mappings.
i.e., If a revenue type is related to a specific claimant, the system reads only the claimant-specific sheet.
 ** The revenue type, Domain
Certification-related mappings in one sheet. 
All other revenue/tax types in separate sheets.
Additional Parameters as reference implementation in GL Decision Table [https://jira.intrasoft-intl.com/browse/IRM-37721] 
 ** Considerations : Customers may also add a rule, to read for every FT,  2 or more sheets,  as the rules sheet may split per Ledger.   (The system reads from two or more sheets per FT, e.g. one per Ledger.) 
Other cases may include parameters to split on segment type category/subcategory or revenue type details and some of these details may be also captured in data areas.


+2. Expandability+

*E) Customers are able to use custom in process implementation*
Be able to adjust a custom implementation in process to run in order  to create journal entries. Interface (as in allocation) to feed the results in Solon Journal entries

 

*Documentation*

All configuration options, split strategies, and rule evaluation logic must be fully documented.

Documentation must include:
 * Usage and Configuration examples
 * Reference implementations
 * Operational guidelines , Performance considerations

*Non functional requirements*

The solution must maintain or improve the product’s:

*Performance* – large datasets and multi-sheet evaluation must not degrade processing times
*Security* – no exposure of sensitive configuration data
*Accessibility* – configuration screens and documentation must remain accessible
*Usability* – splitting logic must be understandable and maintainable by admins
Additionally:
The team must collaborate with domain specialists to validate the above.

All Definition of Done ({*}DoD{*}) criteria must be met.

      .req-seg.oth style.width → OTHER_PCT + '%' and inner text → OTHER_PCT + '%'
      Legend (.req-leg-pct):
        1st (GRC)   → GRC_TOTAL hours in k notation, e.g. '58.3k'
        2nd (GTM)   → GTM_TOTAL hours in k notation, e.g. '4.4k'
        3rd (Other) → OTHER_TOTAL hours in k notation, e.g. '101.3k'
      Source: Requester Stats sheet — sum Estimate by Requester across all PIs.
      Percentages: round( requester_total / sum_all_requesters × 100 ) to nearest integer.
      Do NOT change CSS, class names, legend labels, or element structure.
    '>
